Friends of other aspirants for the posi
tion at once preferred charges against
Daniels, declaring ; that he was a faro
dealer and all . around bad. man. It is
these charges, apparently, that have led
the President to recall the Marshal's
commission he had tendered the Ari
zonan. . , \
Daniels took $250 and went on to "Washi
ington to see the President. A week
later Conn received a dispatch from Dan
iels saying, "I've got the appointment,"
and the papers the next day announced
that Ben Daniels had been appointed
United States Marshal for Arizona.
"Help yourself, Ben,'; he said. "Take
enough to go to Washington and see
Teddy." ;
"I believe 1 can get something from the
President."- he said to Conn, "but I
haven't enough money to go and see
him.".
Conn went to his 'safe and brought out
his gold box.
Daniels was mining in the Magdalena
district in Sonora for some time, and a
few years ago sold a mine for $4000. He
had many friends and his money wa3
given freely, as is the custom on the bor
der, until he was left : without a cent.
Forced by adversity, he went to his old
friend, M. M. Conn, who conducts a
gambling house in Nogales, and told him
he was "broke." ' , .
Goes to See the President.
Daniels was a cowpuncher for some
time in Arizona.- He has been a pros
pector and miner, a meralur of many a
Sheriff's posse in pusuit of outlaws; but
in all his life on the border he has never
had a quarrel, bar one incident in Crow
Canyon, which cost him a portion of his
right ear. Daniels was engaged on a
round-up, of cattle and one night in camp
a cowpuncher attacked him. Daniels
tried to throw the fellow off, but in the
scuttle his assailant bit off a piece of his
ear.
He is â¢ regarded as strictly honest, al
though his life has been cast among the
bad men of . the frontier country, i No
doubt the President knew the character
of Daniels, and if he has recalled Danieis'
commission as Marshal it is because he
could not make the people see Daniels
as he is. .
On the border Daniols 'is regarded as a
man ' oi exceptional nerve and daring.
Av hen he nrst came to Arizona he
"trained" with George Hayes, the noted
cowboy and border "gunngnter." Daniels
and Hayes are still good friends. Dan
iels' character is littingiy described . by
one of his iriends, who says: â¢
"Daniels will shoot a man if he has to,
but he won't steal/'
Noted for His Baring.
It is eaid Daniels saved the life of Col
onel itooseveii on one occasion. A ripan
ish sharpshooter was airecting his iviau
ser buiiets at the leader of the Rough
Kiders. Daniels had oeen sent forward
as a scout by Roosevelt arm found tne
sharpshooter in a tree, trying to get ac
curate range with his rifle to Kill tne col
onel. Daniels picked the" shurpsnooter
out of the tree before he. could harm the
commander.'
The story of Daniels is a border ro
mance, Ha sequel being the recognition
by President Koosavelt of tne iormer
cowpunciier, wno lougnt valiantly on San

Salvation Army Wedding.
A unique wedding was celebrated â¢ last
night by the Salvation Army in the hall
at the corner of Post street and Grant
avenue. The little hall was prettily deco
rated In green and white. The bride was
Bertha A. Barnstark and the groom Hen
ry C. Keyser. They were attended by Cap
tain Jessie Gibson and Mr. Johnson. Each
wore the regulation army suit.

Haas Bros., Pennell-Suydam Company
an'd other creditors of E. A. Wilson of
Santa Rosa filed a petition yesterday in
the United States District Court asking
that he be declared an Involuntary Insol
vent. The petition alleges that Wilson
had committed an act of insolvency by
transferring $700 to the Bank of Santa
Rosa with the Intention of making the
bank a preferred creditor. It is further
alleged that he owes the petitioning cred
itors $2500.
Involuntary Insolvency.
John M. Pettigrew and Hilbert Bros,
were admitted to membership in the or
ganization.
Resolutions were adopted requesting
Congress to officially adopt the metric
system before January 1, 1904. It was also
decided to request the Congressional dele
gates from this State to exert themselves
toward securing the establishment of light
and fog signals at Point Buchon and Â¦ a
fog whistle at the entrance of Carquinez
Straits. ;
The Board of Supervisors is to be re
quested by the chamber to appropriate
$20,<XO for the purpose of making a worthy
exhibit at the St. Louis fair.
Appropriate resolutions on the death of
Rear Admiral Kimberly, wh<j waa an hon
orary member of the chamber, were
adopted.
The board of directors of the Chamber
of Commerce held their regular monthly
meeting yesterday. The vote of the mem
bers of the chamber on the matter of the
exclusion of Chinese of the commercial
class was the most Important subject for
consideration. The count of the ballots
showed that 329 firms had voted In favor
of and 51 'against the resolution asking
Congress to enact a law Â¦which would per
mit the free entrance into this country of
Chinese merchants, buyers, sellers, man
agers and agents. A memorial was ac
cordingly prepared which Â¦ will be for
warded to the President and the members
of the California delegation at Washing
ton, D. C.
Free Entrance of Chinese of
Commercial Class.

CHAMBER OF COMMERCE
HOLDS MONTHLY MEETING
W. H. Mills made a striking assertion
concerning the inactivity of San Francis
co in exploiting the resources of the ter
ritory lying north of Tehachapi. and
therefore tributary to this city. He said
that the advertising that Los Angeles had
secured for the southern portion of the
State was an asset the value of which he
estimated Â¦ at $10,000,000. In twelve years
the State Board of Trade had expended
$250,000 in advertising the State. â¢ In fact
it had been the only agency to advertise
this part of California. In the same pe
riod the great city of San Francisco
Â¦which had an assessment roll of the total
amount of $500,000,000. had not expended
more than $10,000 to advertise the interior
F. McKenzle, representing Commission
er Sedgwlck, invited the board to send a
California exhibit to the Crystal Palace
exhibition in- London, but the request was
denied because there were not funds
available.
Director Wooster and others debated
the best means of having the advantages
of the State brought to the notice of the
people of the Bast. On motion of Woos
ter, thanks were voted to Tne Call, the
Chronicle and the Sacramento Record-
Union for recently .calling attention to
the resources of the central and northern
portions of the State.
In addition. to this the State Board of
Trade, at the meeting yesterday after
noon, received a preliminary report con
cerning the exhibition to be made at St.
LouLs. The committee met yesterday
forenoon and continued in session some
hours. The fact appeared that the coun
ties which are asked to furnish funds to
secure an adequate representation of the
State at St. Louis desire to have county
exhibits, that localities may be definitely
identified with the products that are
shown. The committee was given more
time to make inquiries concerning a large
number of details.
Interior of State Poorly Advertised.
The effect of this move will be to pro
vide a permanent exposition of the re
sources of the State in the most public
place in San Francisco where it must
daily be seen by thousands. Another ad
vantage will be in having an exhibit of
comprehensive scope always under the
control of the State Board of Trade that
can be moved, if necessary, to any place
-where great crowds congregate, as in the
case of a national convention in the Me
chanics' Pavilion, or other rallying point.
'J hjs will not do away with the county
exhibits that are now on the upper floor
of the ferry building, where they occupy
a much greater space than is ever allot
ted to any one State at a world's exposi
tion.
Steps were taken yesterday that will
probably result In placing a large, com
plete and representative exhibit of the
products of the State of California In the
grand nave of the ferry building, at the
foot of Market street, where they may
be seen by every person who enters into
or passes out of San Francisco by the
Market-street gateway. The State Board
of Harbor Commissioners have signified
their willingness to allot the necessary
space in the grand nave. Yesterday af
ternoon the State Board of Trade, on mo
tion of W. H. Mills, instructed Secretary
Filcber to proceed to collect the exhibit
for the board. Mills, In making the mo
tion, said that the State exhibit should
be complete and that even* industry In
the State should be represented. The
t>oard readily and unanimously adopted
the idea.

BOARD RESUMES
WATER INQUIRY
Schussler Tells of New
Sources Acquired by ,
The investigation into the operations of
the Spring Valley Water Works, prepara
tory to fixing the rates to be charged for
water, was resumed last night by thÂ«
Beard of Supervisors. The company sub
mitted maps ; of all the properties owned
by the company in the various countle3.
They, showed that the company has fifty
seven pieces of property in actual use. 1
Chief Engineer Schussler demonstrated
by means of a large map the several res
ervoirs and water sources owned by the
company. Schussler went into considera
ble detail 'regarding' the new Alairteda
Creek system in the Livermore Valley
recently acquired by the company.
Schussler said the system at present sup
plied lO.OOO.UOO gallons of water dally to
dan' Francisco.
Schuasler told of another corporation
called the Suburban Water Company, or
ganized in Alameda County to deal with
iarmers and others who Insisted on be
ing furnished with water in return for
rights of way. He said the Suburban
Company was controlled by the Spring
Valley Company. Mayor Schmitz desireU
to know* the exact relations between the
two corporations and Schussler explained
that the" Spring Valley Company organ
ized the Suburban i Company to supply
consumers in other counties, as the
Spring Valley Company could only sup
piy the city of San .Francisco with water.
Brandenstein objected to the company
listing as one of its properties the Ala
meda system, from which water was sup
plied to other counties. Brandenstein held
that the entire system should not be recK
oned as an asset of the company upon
which an income should be allowed.
Braunhart objected to a clause con
tained in Schusaler's statement that the
last | Board of Supervisors had held a
secret meeting on February 23, 1901, when
the water rates were fixed. Schussler de
clared that he had not been heard at the
meeting and that he had intended to give
testimony as to under-valuations and
omissions in the report. Brandenstein
held that the evidence was all in at the
time and called on Schuasler to retract
his charge that a secret meeting had teen
held. Schussler agreed to strike out the
word "secret," but the board held that
there had been no meeting:â only a con
ference. Schussler finally withdrew the
charge altogether. M â.',_, .
The board accepted Schussler's invita
tion to visit the Livermore Valley system
next Sunday and adjourned to meet next
Tuesday night to continue the inquiry.
Policemen ,<m Their Muscle.
The police officers of this city will be
on their muscle next Monday night at the
Hall of Justice, when the Civil Service
Commission will conduct a physical ex
eniinatlon of those who desire to take the
examination for promotion, to positions of
corporal in the department. . , The exam
ination will be conducted by Drs. Bazet,
Buckley and Ward, the last two being
members of the Board of Health. About
two hundred policemen have filed.appli
cations to take the examination for pro
motions. The oral and written examina
tions will be held In the auditorium of the
Girls' High School February 23 at 1 p. m.
Camera Club Entertains Friends.
The California Camera'Club held- ;Its
monthly meeting and entertainment last
night at the club" rooms, in the Academy
of Sciences building. The seating capacity
of the rooms was quite inadequate to ac
commodate the throng of visitors. The
following programme was rendered:
Slides from the Montreal and Toronto
camera clubs; solo. Miss Bertha Campe;
reading, Miss Charlotte Graeber; Leonard
McAvoy, in just a -bit of ragtime; Mi33
Claire Hosier, recitation: Mrs. Parker .se
lections on the piano; Mrs. Hobson, vocal
selections- . â¢ .
